        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2493899179" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer161001113138734192"><strong>Rating:</strong> 3.5/5 stars<br/><br/>Well my friends, the time has come and the games are over.<br/><br/>I'm going to keep this review relatively short because if you've read any of the Caraval books you already know that just about anything can be a spoiler. If you have not read the first two books read this review at your own risk.<br/><br/>Here's the thing, I wasn't expecting to love this more than <em>Legendary</em>, however, a 3.5 rating stings a little bit. Not that it's a low rating but it's more of a <em>"meh"</em> rating and I never thought </span>
  <span id="freeText161001113138734192" style="display:none"><strong>Rating:</strong> 3.5/5 stars<br /><br />Well my friends, the time has come and the games are over.<br /><br />I'm going to keep this review relatively short because if you've read any of the Caraval books you already know that just about anything can be a spoiler. If you have not read the first two books read this review at your own risk.<br /><br />Here's the thing, I wasn't expecting to love this more than <em>Legendary</em>, however, a 3.5 rating stings a little bit. Not that it's a low rating but it's more of a <em>"meh"</em> rating and I never thought one of these books would fall into that category. I was a little nervous how this book was going to pan out since there is no Caraval game, but I figured now Tella and Scarlett were playing a bigger game so how bad could it be? And it's not that it was bad, but just like I mentioned in my <em>Legendary</em> review, this got <strong>REALLY</strong> redundant. So much of this story is essentially the girls repeating what tasks they need to complete to save each other...and the world as they know it.<br /><br />As usual the world-building and descriptions are <strong>TOP NOTCH</strong> and continue to suck you into the story three books later. Plus, this book as a love triangle (which normally I hate) but oof - the tension was unreal. I was sweating 85% of this book for that alone. But unfortunately, all these things can't carry the story on it's back. I honestly, think the reason why I ended up giving this book a 3.5 rating and not lower is because I was happy with the ending... for the characters. Was I happy with the ending? Considering it was a thousand times less anticlimactic than the first two books, not really. I was actually a little shocked at the predicability of the ending. But alas, my heart was happy with the resolution of the love triangle so I'll just shut up about the rest.<br /><br />Before you think I hated this book entirely, because I really haven't said anything positive yet, I promise I didn't hate it! I loved the fact that Scarlett stepped up to the plate a little bit more in this book and was willing to take the risks needed to <em>"get shit done"</em>, since I need to be vague and all. I also enjoyed how these story gave us a better look at the Fates, their history, and answered more questions about Tella and Scarlett's mother. There are still plenty of plot twists that make this book an enjoyable read even if it does feel like there is a bit of a disconnect from the first two books.<br /><br /><b>Favorite Quotes</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“Occasionally, there are minutes that get extra seconds. Moments so precious the universe stretches to make additional room for them, and this was one of them. People don’t get pauses like these very often. Some people never receive them at all.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“A true queen’s power isn’t in her crown, my little love. It’s here.” Her mother placed a hand over her heart.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“I'm the villain, even in my own story.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />All in all, while I'm sad to see these characters and this world go, I do have to admit that it is probably the best to say goodbye to them. The games were fun while they lasted but all good things must come to an end!<br /><br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishchicksblog.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookishchick" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishchick_/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="161001113138734192" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2751627828" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2751627828" />
    <a title="Amy Risner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13507409-amy-risner"><img alt="Amy Risner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563900231p2/13507409.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2751627828?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy Risner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy Risner" href="/user/show/13507409-amy-risner">Amy Risner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13507409-amy-risner?shelf=2019-books">2019-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13507409-amy-risner?shelf=2019-arcs">2019-arcs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2751627828" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8104066852055063127"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1557970527i/27516341._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/> <i>ARC provided by Flatiron Books in exchange for an honest review.</i><br/><br/>1) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1903031548?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Caraval</a> ★★★★<br/>2) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2316059473?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Legendary</a> ★★★★<br/><br/>This review pains me to write because I was truly expecting a 5 star read.<br/><br/>I have always thought highly of this series. I loved how Caraval focused on a game and the actors within the game. I loved how Legendary expanded that world and introduced us to the Fates. I truly believe this series could’ve just been a duology; extend Legendary to be a slightly longer book, tie up some loose ends, and call it</span>
  <span id="freeText8104066852055063127" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1557970527i/27516341._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <i>ARC provided by Flatiron Books in exchange for an honest review.</i><br><br>1) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1903031548?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Caraval</a> ★★★★<br>2) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2316059473?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Legendary</a> ★★★★<br><br>This review pains me to write because I was truly expecting a 5 star read.<br><br>I have always thought highly of this series. I loved how Caraval focused on a game and the actors within the game. I loved how Legendary expanded that world and introduced us to the Fates. I truly believe this series could’ve just been a duology; extend Legendary to be a slightly longer book, tie up some loose ends, and call it a wrap. I really don’t understand the point of Finale at all.<br><br>Finale introduces us to a new villain which… seems like an odd time to bring in a new villain. We already met Jacks in Legendary, and in my opinion, he was the perfect “bad guy.” But we get introduced to the ACTUAL villain who is a Fate. And this Fate wants to destroy basically everyone and take Legend’s place. I just really didn’t understand the point of him at all and he was so “mustache twirly” that I had to roll my eyes at all his scenes.<br><br>So let’s talk about Tella and Scarlett. In this book the POV’s alternate between the two sisters, which I actually did like because we got to follow their own little journeys within the story. However, Scarlett was so childish in this book I JUST CANNOT. From the very beginning of the book she decides she wants to string Julian along, and then have Julian and Nicolas compete for her? What kind of childish game is this? I truly do not understand her motivations behind this AT ALL.<br><br>Tella is my favorite of the two sisters but she also did some things that were questionable. She kept seeking solace from Jacks, who is, you know… a villain… and would then be surprised that he *gasp* did a villainous thing. Girl, why? Also, Jacks literally tries to give her a heart attack in order to get what he wants from Legend, but then later tells Tella he “didn’t mean to” and would never hurt her? Excuse me? But you literally just gave her a heart attack, dude. I was always Team Jacks but that scene was so unnecessary to me.<br><br>And speaking of Jacks (who was my favorite character from Legendary.) His character really got reduced down to be a minor side character who only showed up at convenient times to sweep Tella off her feet. I truly didn’t understand his purpose and felt zero closure with him.<br><br>I was also really excited to be introduced to the other Fates, but they all also felt like very minor side characters who didn’t seem to play a pivotal role in the entire story.<br><br>Here’s the thing: I’ve always loved the world of Caraval, but in Finale I felt like most of the time we were being TOLD. It’s full of characters speaking in long paragraphs <b>telling</b> us about the history of something or about another character. It really dragged and made me lose focus. I don’t want to be told everything; I want to <b>see</b> it. Also I refuse to even acknowledge the time-travel loophole because that’s my least favorite trope used to tie up a loose end.<br><br>This was my most anticipated release of 2019 and I am just kind of feeling neutral about how it all ended? I didn’t hate it, but I just didn’t love it either. I know my review sounds super ranty, but I loved being back in the world and with these characters again. I will also forever love Dante because he’s such a sweet guy. Also I think Stephanie Garber is the loveliest human and I will still read everything she writes. I guess I can hope there will be a spin-off for this series?<br><br><a href="https://acourtofcrownsandquills.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/acourtofcrownsandquills/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://www.twitter.com/crownsandquills" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://youtube.com/c/acourtofcrownsandquills" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8104066852055063127" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2751088657" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2751088657" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2751088657?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=awesome-heroines">awesome-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=alternating-pov">alternating-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=unforgettable-male-leads">unforgettable-male-leads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=could-read-over-and-over-again">could-read-over-and-over-again</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2751088657" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4537144915343453049">And here we are-the end. There’s just something so magical about this series that goes beyond the actual, well, magic. The words transport you. The world makes you so thirsty for more. The boys are just so addicting and drag you in, even if you don’t want to…and <b>the relationships make you stay</b>.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1558544808ra/27556199.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I wish I could say that I wasn’t as big a fool for this series as everyone else…but I am. I am so trash for it and I just can’t seem to stop searching and fighting and clawing my way to all the editions of</span>
  <span id="freeText4537144915343453049" style="display:none">And here we are-the end. There’s just something so magical about this series that goes beyond the actual, well, magic. The words transport you. The world makes you so thirsty for more. The boys are just so addicting and drag you in, even if you don’t want to…and <b>the relationships make you stay</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1558544808ra/27556199.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I wish I could say that I wasn’t as big a fool for this series as everyone else…but I am. I am so trash for it and I just can’t seem to stop searching and fighting and clawing my way to all the editions of it I can muster up. I can admit it’s gotten a bit out of hand, but it’s been so fun I can’t say I even care. My husband, however…he may disagree. The whimsical feeling and the high stakes fun make this book and series something that I don’t often find anymore. And I can’t say that it’s all perfect-which is why I’m JUST NOW on the Caraval special UK edition bandwagon-but there’s just something so dazzling that finally stuck it’s claws into me-<b>Too bad it took me years to figure out how much I loved it</b>. Cue eyeroll.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1558544808ra/27556200.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I literally cannot say much about this story because I feel like everyone will know what happens if I do. We all know there will be romantic angst. We all know Julian and Scarlett have some things to work out (and, I’m sorry, but their story, arc, and ending were far more satisfying than any other in this book, for me). We all know Tella and-ahem-are working through major ‘I can’t be your hero’ vibes (ohh but I do so love it *heart eyes*). But aside from that, I’d be doing a disservice to all if I gave too much away.<br><br>So, I’ll do my BEST to capture what made this final book like crack to me.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1558544808i/27556201._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The romantic peril was just…<b>out of this world fantastic</b>. I was drooling from the declarations and pleas and cries and…OKAY I’VE SAID TOO MUCH BUT DAMN IT CAN YOU BLAME ME? Okay. Rerouting. I digress. Back to business-It was spectacular. But it really shined with one couple-And I will reread my favorite moments with this element so many times my iPad will start to smoke. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1540807422ra/26515346.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And the story. I really enjoyed where it went, in this one. Kind of. Welll…Yeah. I did and didn’t. That is one of my two biggest pet peeves. I will spoiler both. But, in general, for most of this book, I was a goner for every little thing. But, the end. The villain-<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[This is BY FAR one of my least favorite ‘fights’ against a villain. Like…is that <i>really</i> how we wanted this epic story, this evil dude, to end? To Die? It basically ends with a realization, a lecture, and a quick stab…and it’s FLIPPING OVER! ‘You’ve been a badddd boy! Now DIE!’ <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I just…my heart. I will say, though, I calmed down enough to re-read the whole ending because I was sooo tired when I read it the first time and it DID make a difference. I still think…what I think…but it wasn’t so bad that I need to de-star it.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1558544808ra/27556202.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And I would be remiss if I didn’t talk about the men in this story (Tella is awesome, Scarlett is awesome, but <b>the boys keep me coming back for more</b>). Julian truly stepped up his game in this one. His heart was literally on his sleeve and I think that if anyone had a problem or was bored by him before (who even ARE you people?) you won’t be now. He shines. And my heart could hardly contain his love. And the other boy, Dante…What a flippin’ turd. And, also, why do I love him so much? He’s mysterious and sacrificial and even though he can be evasive, elusive, and altogether a flighty turd, <b>he is utterly in awe and has utter devotion to Tella</b>, and my heartstrings sing and flutter when he is around. Part 2 spoiler-<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[His story disappointed me. He deserved as epic of a story as Julian. Julian was sacrificial on all fronts. He had a dramatic storyline. His love story ended with a bang. Yes, we get a confession of love by Legend, in the end-and it’s glorious-but his romantic peril was more at the beginning, and wonderful, yet at the end he was just in a sad little cage and it made my heart hurt he didn’t get to be a part of that scene in a monumental way. After everything, the fact that Dante and Tella’s story was way more dramatic, way more perilistic, way more, I don’t know, twisty turny, we get left high and dry, in the end. And I just thought they deserved more, because I think they are technically the more favorited couple. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. And the jealousy-OMG. I must say….I do love some jealousy. And the cute way it’s handled-by both-it makes my heart soar.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1558544808ra/27556203.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So, yeah, it’s not perfect, but it was close to perfect for <i>me</i>. These characters are like my family now, and I truly never want to leave this world. Not many series make me wish for more (if ANY), but this is one of them that I could read about for years. Stephanie Garber has created an alternate universe that has enchanted the world, readers around the nation, and made us apart of the whimsical and dangerous world of Caraval. I only wish I could go see her on tour, but that’s okay-<s>I have some great friends</s> I have a great friend who has my back and is taking my books to be signed. I am a Caraval gal now, and I am just so sad this is the last book where I get to see these four wonderful characters. I will continue to read them again and again, and <b>there’s something magical about that in and of itself</b>.<br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a title="Star-Crossed Book Blog" href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" width="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1516600667i/24898353._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>

</u><br><a title="Instagram" href="https://www.instagram.com/starcrossedbookblog/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_2415417880" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2415417880" />
    <a title="Sara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1170391-sara"><img alt="Sara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590218363p2/1170391.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2415417880?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/1170391-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781473666801" href="/book/show/39071288-finale">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=library-loan">library-loan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2415417880" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12965669421177241235">Finale is the conclusion to the YA fantasy, carnival, colourful Caraval series, and follows almost immediately on from the conclusion of Legendary. We find Tella, abandoned by Legend and mourning her apparent unrequited love, and we have Scarlett mooning after Julian who left to undertaking some ‘serious business’ for Legend. There’s also the threat of the released Fates, immortals bound by their desire to destroy and play hateful games with the citizens of Valenda. <br/><br/>My overall impression started</span>
  <span id="freeText12965669421177241235" style="display:none">Finale is the conclusion to the YA fantasy, carnival, colourful Caraval series, and follows almost immediately on from the conclusion of Legendary. We find Tella, abandoned by Legend and mourning her apparent unrequited love, and we have Scarlett mooning after Julian who left to undertaking some ‘serious business’ for Legend. There’s also the threat of the released Fates, immortals bound by their desire to destroy and play hateful games with the citizens of Valenda. <br /><br />My overall impression started off quite positive. I enjoyed the previous novels in the series, although I found the writing quite immature at times, but I found the overall feel of the books to be good. There was a certain aura of mystery and intrigue with the Caraval games that pulled me into the story. This started out in a similar vein, with a couple of love triangle tropes thrown in for good measure, that I found interesting. Jacks in particular I really loved reading about, as we see him struggle with his obsession and lust for Tella war agains some deeper feelings of unrequited love and heartbreak. I felt at times he was severely underused, often sidelined for the more boring straightforward and obvious love between Tella and Legend. He seemed to pop up as a plot device to either rescue or help Tella, or advance the plot in a rather unsophisticated way. <br /><br />That was another issue I had here. There’s no cleverness and subtlety to the plot. It’s all obvious and predictable, with no surprises. The villain, Gavriel, feels very lacklustre too. He’s very black and white, with an overall arc that feels quite primitive and underdeveloped. He feels very one dimensional, and because of this the plot suffers badly. Add to this the several plot threads and characters that are dropped suddenly and not concluded properly (the witch who made Legend, the Count, Tella’s future...I could go on) and the weak and rushed ending, and you can begin to see how I really struggled to finish this. It just felt like a completely different book with different characters to the previous novels. <br /><br />Tella, who I grew to love in the previous novel, seems to regress into a mopey girl here. She spends 90% of the novel either shouting at Jacks, mooning over Legend or running aimlessly around the city trying to learn anything about destroying the Fates. There’s no depth to her character at all, and her relationship with Scarlett feels forced. Scarlett I found more relatable and genuine. Her feelings for Julian seem more realistic, although the whole subplot with the Count felt pointless. If anything it detracted from the main story and bogged down the pace. I could have done without it. I also could have done with more from Legend. This immortal, magical man, is reduced to almost nothing of his former self. He’s lost that illusion, mysterious edge that made him interesting and here it’s replaced with a love drunk fool. <br /><br />Finale, for me, felt very ‘meh’. The writing just isn’t strong enough to hold up a story that consists of weak, underdeveloped villains and characters that are barely recognisable in a plot hole heavy story. I think this should have remained as a duology, because I honestly think there isn’t enough story to tell here.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12965669421177241235" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2845052402" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2845052402" />
    <a title="R.F. Gammon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62220551-r-f-gammon"><img alt="R.F. Gammon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556208215p2/62220551.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2845052402?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="R.F. Gammon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="R.F. Gammon" href="/user/show/62220551-r-f-gammon">R.F. Gammon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2845052402" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6136293147660132007">OKAY! I finally got to read the last 30 pages of this after returning it to the library and going on vacation in the middle of reading it (ugghhhh). So now it's time for an actual review!<br/><br/>Where even to begin?<br/><br/>I loved that the focus was back on Scarlett, and that she and Julian have an actual relationship in this one, unlike in <i>Legendary</i>, where I'm pretty sure they were only present to provide some background angst on top of Tella's foreground angst. I really, really did not like the second book in</span>
  <span id="freeText6136293147660132007" style="display:none">OKAY! I finally got to read the last 30 pages of this after returning it to the library and going on vacation in the middle of reading it (ugghhhh). So now it's time for an actual review!<br /><br />Where even to begin?<br /><br />I loved that the focus was back on Scarlett, and that she and Julian have an actual relationship in this one, unlike in <i>Legendary</i>, where I'm pretty sure they were only present to provide some background angst on top of Tella's foreground angst. I really, really did not like the second book in this series, and I think it's because I didn't really love Tella as a character. I mean, she's fine, but Scarlett is my favorite for sure, and I love Julian way more than I like Legend or Jacks.<br /><br />Paradise was such a fascinating and compelling character, definitely my favorite part of this story, although I liked the Fallen Star as well. All the Fates were super interesting, if I'm being honest. Except for Jacks. I did NOT like the way he was romanticized--he was nothing but dangerous and evil and he's that sort of "love interest" that scares me because he's so controlling. It's definitely depicted as dangerous? But also he's SO HOT and he can manipulate Tella into thinking and feeling whatever he wants her to and I don't like that. At alllll. <br /><br />I guess that's my biggest problem with this series--I don't love Tella. Just as a character. She's flighty and immature and the type of manic dream girl I don't like AT ALL. She's confident, but not in a good way. I just don't like her. We do not connect on any level. That's probably the real problem I have with this series as a whole. Also, her struggle comes entirely from her love triangle (Yeah, there's stuff about her mama, but we all know that the only plot Tella really gets is DANTE OR JACKS???!!! PICK A DANGER BOY, ANY DANGER BOY, IT'S ALL GOOD!)<br /><br />*is not a fan*<br /><br />Some smol things I did love though:<br />-Scarlett+Julian (yes please)<br />-The magic Fated dress<br />-The empress!<br />-The Fates are so interesting and I love them<br />-The aesthetic and the writing<br />-Time travel is weird as always<br />-The covers of this series are so prettyyyyy<br />-Good sister relationships<br /><br />Overall? Perfectly fine finale (pun intended) to a perfectly meh series. Tella is a downside; I adore Scarlett and Julian both. I despise Jacks. I don't love Dante. I love Paradise. Everyone else? Meh.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6136293147660132007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

		<td>
      
			<a class="actionLink" href="/topic/show/21370906-spoiler-question-about-tella-and-legend-s-relationship">*Spoiler* Question about Tella and Legend&#39;s relationship</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('f4HlWgOAzOJ2Mwmc3FTso23BvNLJq8CtTwv7rvX+5W6mWgI2/r70IqJl/LFTrdcPx04oMkxtCgoHC4LYPmgYuQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Qg4Ze7CA64+VE0NfzUhCjpV6f5wttVnRqbDT5dKR9neb1f4XTb7TT0FFtnJCsXkiP/XrfKhzk3bhsKqTGQcLoA==')})
  }
